  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e1d454bc-16f2-4923-9af6-2dae2ce21a47'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33246624-mariel?shelf=series">series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1042840851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14936668841787277284"><br/>Well how to begin? I've heard AMAZING things about this middle grade trilogy but unfortunately it didn't work for me. I wasn't expecting a love triangle and it was one of the weirdest I've ever read where both male characters knew about each other but didn't care as long as they were with HER. SERIOUSLY? It was too focus in the romance and I was sold this would be a fantasy world I'd love. Though the world building wasn't THAT bad I couldn't stand the love triangle!!!<br/><br/>A ver, por dónde empiezo?? H</span>
  <span id="freeText14936668841787277284" style="display:none"><br />Well how to begin? I've heard AMAZING things about this middle grade trilogy but unfortunately it didn't work for me. I wasn't expecting a love triangle and it was one of the weirdest I've ever read where both male characters knew about each other but didn't care as long as they were with HER. SERIOUSLY? It was too focus in the romance and I was sold this would be a fantasy world I'd love. Though the world building wasn't THAT bad I couldn't stand the love triangle!!!<br /><br />A ver, por dónde empiezo?? Había escuchado fantásticas cosas sobre esta trilogía pero desafortunademente no funcionó para mí. No estaba esperando un triángulo amoroso y fue uno de los triángulos más raros que he leído donde los personajes masculinos sabían de la existencia del otro pero no les importaba siempre que estuvieran con ella. EN SERIO? Estuvo muy enfocado en el romance y a mi me habían vendido este libro como una fantasía que iba a amar. Aunque el desarrollo del mundo no estuvo TAN mal no pude soportar el triángulo amoroso</span>
  <a data-text-id="14936668841787277284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Big murderer guy who is also a kid but older enough than her so it's already creepy. But it's e</span>
  <span id="freeText4450170187107527344" style="display:none">I first read this book in middle school but the 3rd volume never got translated to my native language and at that time I couldn't read in any other language. Now I speak Spanish, and I was excited to read a book in that language.<br />So I started it with a lot of enthusiasm and well, while the world building is kind of interesting... what is it with the big murderer guy being attracted to the little girl?? Big murderer guy who is also a kid but older enough than her so it's already creepy. But it's extremely worse than that since he's literally a murderer! The way his attraction is described is absolutely disgusting. And Victoria being attracted to him as well while the guy literally killed the parents of his best friend, while Vic is just in general a normal sweet girl? It makes no sense and it's absolutely horrible.<br />Now I'm thinking of people reading that in middle school. Imagine if they meet someone horrible irl and still like them because "it's okay i'm just like victoria" no!!! It's just extremely dangerous and the author is completely irresponsible for writing something like that.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735247616" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7759038877843376160">My first attempt at reading a Spanish book series. Learning Spanish has opened my door to new stories and adventures I’d never heard of before. And this first one, La Resistencia by Laura Gallego García, was a real treat. A mix of Star Wars and Star Trek, the first book in the Memorias de Idhún series was full of jaw dropping surprises. Literally a twist at the end of every chapter. This young adult book follows three troubled teenagers as they join the Resistance to find the lost dragon and uni</span>
  <span id="freeText7759038877843376160" style="display:none">My first attempt at reading a Spanish book series. Learning Spanish has opened my door to new stories and adventures I’d never heard of before. And this first one, La Resistencia by Laura Gallego García, was a real treat. A mix of Star Wars and Star Trek, the first book in the Memorias de Idhún series was full of jaw dropping surprises. Literally a twist at the end of every chapter. This young adult book follows three troubled teenagers as they join the Resistance to find the lost dragon and unicorn before the evil Ashran el Nigromante can get his hands on them. And to bring peace to Idhún once again. Laura Gallego García is now one of my favorite authors, and I couldn’t wait to rush out to buy the second book in her series. I highly recommend this book if you like unpredictability.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7759038877843376160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10549164228789735028">Good book, innovative and interesting. <br/>However, it is way too predictable. You know what is going to happen and the main characters dont. I am not that smart, and the characters are not that stupid. It makes half book a bit boring.<br/>This said, the book as a whole is quite absorbing and is easy to read (especially because you get drawn into the story).<br/>I will read the second part for two reasons: i want to follow the story and i want to see if the book becomes less predictable.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12708456514776360122">I read this when I was 9 years-old (or 8, I don't really remember), I loved it then. Now, it's a bit icky. The writing style is bit juvenile for me and the characters are extremely young, I don't know what Laura Gallego Garcia was thinking. There's a time skip and even then the female main character is just 15 and her two love interests are 16. I wish they would be around 19-20, because it wouldn't be as creepy as it seems. Like I know 15 years-old and 17 years-old and they are worlds apart. I g</span>
  <span id="freeText12708456514776360122" style="display:none">I read this when I was 9 years-old (or 8, I don't really remember), I loved it then. Now, it's a bit icky. The writing style is bit juvenile for me and the characters are extremely young, I don't know what Laura Gallego Garcia was thinking. There's a time skip and even then the female main character is just 15 and her two love interests are 16. I wish they would be around 19-20, because it wouldn't be as creepy as it seems. Like I know 15 years-old and 17 years-old and they are worlds apart. I get it that girls are usually more mature, but still. I guess it justifies some of the most childish and immature decisions.<br /><br />I should rate this one star, because the writing and the plot is abysmally poor, but it gets an extra star for nostalgia value. When I was 8-9 and I had no discerning eye, I loved this. We all have a series like that. </span>

<div id="review_710322385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/710322385" />
    <a title="Marina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23618254-marina"><img alt="Marina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379342023p2/23618254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/710322385?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marina" href="/user/show/23618254-marina">Marina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781416947295" href="/book/show/16074655-memorias-de-idhun">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer710322385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14315216830939998051">This book hooks you from the first page when Jack came home from school and he found his parents dead on the floor. He had had the chance to see the assassin. As they made eye contact, Jack thought he was going to die, but then, someone took him to a safe place and saved his life. That place is Limbhad, a shielded territory from evil people who killed wizards that had escaped from Idhun to survive from Ashran, the leader, and the sheks (huge and deadly, flying snakes). In Limbhad there’s a girl,</span>
  <span id="freeText14315216830939998051" style="display:none">This book hooks you from the first page when Jack came home from school and he found his parents dead on the floor. He had had the chance to see the assassin. As they made eye contact, Jack thought he was going to die, but then, someone took him to a safe place and saved his life. That place is Limbhad, a shielded territory from evil people who killed wizards that had escaped from Idhun to survive from Ashran, the leader, and the sheks (huge and deadly, flying snakes). In Limbhad there’s a girl, Victoria, who becomes a good friend of Jack’s. There are also two wizards and together, they form a group that tries to save wizard’s lives who escaped towards the Earth. <br />Ashran and the sheks managed to kill all the unicorns and dragons (the most important creatures in Idhun) except Lunnaris, the unicorn and Yandrak, the dragon. Later on, Jack and Victoria find out that they are the last dragon (Jack) and unicorn (Victoria). Kirtash, the assassin who killed Jack’s parents, was interested in Victoria so one day he proposed to her if she would like to go with him and rule Idhun. Slowly, Victoria was falling in love with Kirtash, even though he took away the lives of many people. There was something about him that amazed Victoria although she doubted if he was tricking or fooling her. Later, Jack and Victoria found out that Kirtash is half shek half human when he suddenly attacks Jack and turns into a flying snake. He was about to kill Jack when Victoria shielded him and that’s when she started to fall in love with Jack too. Jack and Kirtash become enemies, but they try hard not to kill each other because they know they would hurt Victoria if any of them died. On many of the occasions that Kirtash had to kill Victoria, he didn’t do it and he betrayed his father, Ashran, just to save her life and be with her. <br />I really liked this book because it was really interesting and it can be read by both girls and boys and people who like fantasy. It has fights, adventures, romance, tragedy, betrayal and mystery, so it’s pretty complete. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14315216830939998051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1017464650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1017464650" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1017464650?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelina" href="/user/show/28448203-evelina">Evelina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1017464650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8636337935464212315">I liked the beginning of the trilogy and I will probably finish it only to see how it ends. It is a young adult fantasy book so I wish I had found it when I was a teenager, I feel I would be so much more involved in it than now. <br/>In this story, the protagonist, Jack, is a child leading normal, ordinary life until one day he returns home and discovers that his parents were murdered at the hands of two people who even try to kill him too, but he is rescued, and from that moment his life is not the </span>
  <span id="freeText8636337935464212315" style="display:none">I liked the beginning of the trilogy and I will probably finish it only to see how it ends. It is a young adult fantasy book so I wish I had found it when I was a teenager, I feel I would be so much more involved in it than now. <br />In this story, the protagonist, Jack, is a child leading normal, ordinary life until one day he returns home and discovers that his parents were murdered at the hands of two people who even try to kill him too, but he is rescued, and from that moment his life is not the same. He discovers that there is another parallel world apart from this one, filled with magic and fantastic creatures-Indhún. That plot twist sort of reminded me of Harry Potter.<br /><br />Jack is taken to a place called Limbad, a place between Earth and the world of Indhún, by two young men who saved him and who form part of the resistance, Prince Alsan and a magician named Shail, both fighting Ashran the necromancer who has Indhún under his control. They are looking for two pieces that are the only ones that can help them in their fight against the necromancer. Victoria, a young woman who apparently may have a knack for magic also joins the resistance. Jack discovers that his parents were murdered since he belongs to Indhún as well.<br /><br />Kirtash, an antagonist, is a mysterious character who is in charge of hunting down all those refugees who managed to escape Indhún and who now live in hiding on Earth. He was one of the people who murdered Jack's parents and there will be some sort of love triangle between him, Jack and Victoria.<br /><br />The characters are well developed, the plot and their stories become more entwined as the story goes on. The book has fantasy, action, mystery and some romance, dragons, sheks (winged serpents), unicorns and magic. There are some predictable and slow parts, but it was an enjoyable read. This is the first time I am reading a book by Laura Gallego García and it is OK all in all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8636337935464212315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1308408428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308408428" />
    <a title="Isabel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32476084-isabel"><img alt="Isabel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434365769p2/32476084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1308408428?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabel" href="/user/show/32476084-isabel">Isabel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308408428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13563414370992654417">I read this book almost ten years ago. Wow, time goes by so quickly! I was around 13 when it came into my hands. I was at school, it was Friday and the Spanish lesson every Friday was reading. I had forgotten a book, and I was too lazy to go to the library. So I asked my best friend, who was in another class, wether she had a book I could borrow. So she gave me Memorias de Idhun. I was reluctant, as I wasn't much of a reader at that time, and it kind of is a big book. Which now that I think abou</span>
  <span id="freeText13563414370992654417" style="display:none">I read this book almost ten years ago. Wow, time goes by so quickly! I was around 13 when it came into my hands. I was at school, it was Friday and the Spanish lesson every Friday was reading. I had forgotten a book, and I was too lazy to go to the library. So I asked my best friend, who was in another class, wether she had a book I could borrow. So she gave me Memorias de Idhun. I was reluctant, as I wasn't much of a reader at that time, and it kind of is a big book. Which now that I think about it is very strange. That is because when I was younger I read three times as much as my friends at school. Hahaha. Back to the book! I usually lose focus easily. :) When class started, I began reading. <br /><br />By the time I finish the first chapter I was already trapped. I couldn't stop reading. When class finished that day I went to the bookstore to buy it. I needed to know what happened next. And I ended up finishing it in two days! So I couldn't wait for the next book to be released. I was so excited! I even won at school the privilege of going to a meeting with the author, as I was the student who read the most books! ^^<br /><br />The story is amazing, really original. Laura has an ability for words that is rare in writers nowadays. The book traps you. The descriptions are detailed, bright and fresh. She really knows haw to transport you to the Idhun she had in her mind. It's language is easy to read, but it's complex. Spanish is a difficult language, with many tenses and words. And although the language is complex she makes you understand it. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to any young reader. It's great for beginners. And as the trilogy is completed finishing it in a week time is guaranteed! I am not giving it five stars because, now at this stage I've found many better books, at least for me. But I recommend it 100%. If you're a true reader it's a must. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13563414370992654417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4774489608941427126" style="display:none">I read this when I was about 14, or something, and I recall liking it. <span id="freeTextContainer10437018139229653511">Actual rating 3.5 <br/><br/>I remember loving this a few years ago -- the excitement of a fantasy world that's just different enough from other fantasy worlds to be intriguing, while keeping the elements of fantasy that I love (DRAGONS, unicorns, magic, various humanoid species, prophecies). <br/><br/>This book (series) also has one of the few love triangles that don't bother me, although upon rereading this, I realized how one of the boys is actually not that romantic and really just an asshole. I know he improves</span>
  <span id="freeText10437018139229653511" style="display:none">Actual rating 3.5 <br /><br />I remember loving this a few years ago -- the excitement of a fantasy world that's just different enough from other fantasy worlds to be intriguing, while keeping the elements of fantasy that I love (DRAGONS, unicorns, magic, various humanoid species, prophecies). <br /><br />This book (series) also has one of the few love triangles that don't bother me, although upon rereading this, I realized how one of the boys is actually not that romantic and really just an asshole. I know he improves, though, and by the end of the book it's already better, but I'm a little more skeptical and wary of him now than I used to be. <br /><br />Also, the pacing is sometimes a little wonky when the characters seemed to focus more on their love triangle issues than the overarching plot, which makes me like the triangle less.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fIgb95GmkwGuGwdCXqkyYmtwSweu+AeCZQ9Hrn1wJwoAy5ZzZebVX3XFGCaaScERQHqM1CSlbkMvcKGAzBiXAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oL7p4IoR8gl9R/HpUzSdN0W3ovmxLrDPoWPoIZd0uPfc/WRkflG0V6aZ7o2X1G5Ebr1lKjtz2Q7rHA4PJhwI/g==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a">About Laura Gallego García</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3401673511737339819">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br/><br/>Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began.</span>
  <span id="freeText3401673511737339819" style="display:none">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br /><br />Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began. <br /><br />Finis Mundi was followed, chronologically, by (only mentioning the ones that achieved notable popularity)the ''Crónicas de la Torre'' saga, ''The Legend of the Wandering King'', ''Memories of Idhún'' saga, ''La Emperatriz de los Etéreos'' and the ''Alas Negras'' saga. <br />From all of them, her most popular and internationally recognized work has been the Memorias de Idhún saga. Formed by three books, written between 2004 and 2006, the story (pure fantasy genre) centers in the three main characters: Victoria, Jack and Christian; and the world of Idhún. Dragons, unicorns, magic, prophecies and everything your imagination can lead you to. <br />The saga of Idhún and most of her works have been published to numerous languagues such as English, French, German, Italian, Hungarian, Greek, Portuguese, Corean, Polish, Swedish, Finish, Danish, Rumanian, Turkish...<br /><br />She loves manga comics. Her favourite book of all time is ''The Neverending Story'', though she enjoys reading as well authors such as Tolkien, Weis, Peter Beagle and Coehlo.<br /><br />Currently she combines being a mother and enjoying her family life with the realization of her thesis. She finished this year her last novel, ''Donde los árboles cantan'' (Where the trees sing), which will be published in October 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3401673511737339819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
